Racetrack Dashboard Overview

General Dashboard Information
Dashboard Composition: The dashboard is made up of a grid of widget components. Each has its own function that processes the data from EYECUE server into a visual UI.
Widget Descriptions: All widgets have a detailed explanation of what they do within the designer itself. Simply hover over one in the drop down menu to read its description.
Types of Data: Most widget data comes through IoT/MQTT and is processed by the `data_holder.js` into its relevant objects.
IoT/MQTT Topics:
  • **`/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`**: Contains all averages for a store for the past rolling hour in seconds (e.g., `START`, `ORDER_1`, `PAYMENT`, `DELIVER`, `PULL_FORWARD`, `WAITING`, `OEPE`, `TET` averages and percentages).
  • **`/eyeq/current-hour/{fingermark_id}`**: Provides analytics of the store in the current hour (e.g., `count` of completed vehicles).
  • **`/eyeq/oepe-daily/{fingermark_id}`**: Provides OEPE data since store opened (or 4am for 24h stores), including average and percentage of cars achieving target.
  • **`/eyeq/bar-chart/{fingermark_id}`**: Provides last 36 hours of car counts per hour for a specific store.
Additional Data Sources:
  • **`averageData` Lambda**: Used to call a separate lambda that retrieves all the average data between two time stamps. This data is used to calculate the Throughput of a drivethru. (Soon to be deprecated)
  • **`sixtyMinuteData` Lambda**: Used to get the vehicle count and average time for DTO stores. (Soon to be deprecated)
  • **`getLastShiftData` GraphQL**: Used to get all the counts of a certain day part at a store over the last 6 weeks to calculate the peak 15 goal for the current day part.
ðŸ’¡ When creating new widgets, there is no strict rules as to which widget should fall into which category, as long as it makes common sense.
Time Based Metrics

Widgets that use time as a variable, i.e., counts over the last hour, or target percentages since store opened today.

KPI - From Open

Description: Displays key performance indicators from the store's opening time (or 4am for 24h stores).
How it is calculated: Uses `average` and `percentage` from `/eyeq/oepe-daily/{fingermark_id}`. Percentage is of cars achieving target for that KPI.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/oepe-daily/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Daily (since store open/4am).

KPI - Past Hour

Description: Displays key performance indicators for the past hour.
How it is calculated: Uses `total` count from `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}` (total completed vehicles in rolling hour).
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Real-time (rolling hour).
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: None specific.

KPI - Past 24 Hours

Description: Displays key performance indicators for the past 24 hours.
How it is calculated: Derived from `count` data in `/eyeq/bar-chart/{fingermark_id}` for the last 24 hours.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/bar-chart/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Updates with historical 36-hour data.
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: None specific.

Car Count

Description: Displays the count of cars.
How it is calculated: Uses `count` from `/eyeq/current-hour/{fingermark_id}` (completed vehicles in current hour) or derived from `total` in `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/current-hour/{fingermark_id}` or `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Real-time (current hour).

Peak 15

Description: Displays data related to "Peak 15" performance. It aims to calculate what the peak 15 goal should be for the current day part.
How it is calculated: Retrieves all counts of a certain day part at a store over the last 6 weeks.
Source of data: GraphQL (`getLastShiftData`).
Frequency of update: TBD (likely on daypart change or regularly based on historical data).

  • fm-tst-nzl-2105
Limitations: None specific.

Average Total Time (OEPE/TET)

Description: Displays the average total time for a process, such as Order Entry to Payment Exit (OEPE) or Total Experience Time (TET). This corresponds to the 'OEPE Average last 60' or 'Journey time 60' in some dashboards.
How it is calculated: Uses `oepe.average` or `tet.average` from `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`. Configurable with `targetType` (e.g., `TOTAL_EXPERIENCE_TIME`, `OEFD_TIME`), `targetId`, `title`, `averageId` (e.g., `orderStartToDeliverEndAverage`, `markDeliverEndAverage`), `timeDisplay`, and `target`.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Real-time (rolling hour).
Clients currently using: [+] Show Clients (430)

Limitations: None specific.

Daypart Thruput

Description: Displays throughput for a specific daypart.
How it is calculated: Calculated by `averageData` lambda, which retrieves average data between two timestamps to determine throughput.
Source of data: `averageData` lambda (soon to be deprecated).
Frequency of update: TBD.
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: Restricted to KFC stores.

Daily Thruput

Description: Displays throughput for the entire day.
How it is calculated: Calculated by `averageData` lambda, which retrieves average data between two timestamps to determine throughput.
Source of data: `averageData` lambda (soon to be deprecated).
Frequency of update: TBD.
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: Restricted to KFC stores.
Zone Based Metrics

Widgets that depend on a specific zone of the drive-thru, usually a live representation of what is happening at that section.

Order Average

Description: Displays the average time for the order zone. Can be split into displaying the average times for lane 1 (`ORDER_1`) and 2 (`ORDER_2`) rather than a combined average.
How it is calculated: Uses `ORDER_1` and `ORDER_2` from `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}` for lane-specific or combined averages.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (`/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Live representation (rolling hour).
Clients currently using: [+] Show Clients (390)

Cars In Zones

Description: This widget shows a real-time representation of the number of cars in each zone (Entry, Order, Deliver, and Exit) throughout the drive thru.
How it is calculated: Specific calculation logic not detailed in configuration, but tracks cars per zone.
Source of data: Implied to be from vehicle detection in zones. Topics: `/eyeq/danger-zones/`. Requires `queue-zone` functionality applied to ROIs.
Frequency of update: Real-time representation.
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: Configurable `title`. Supports both a legacy and a UI V3 configuration interface.
Racetrack Widgets

These widgets display a visualization of a racetrack split into separate components so users can display specific sections of the drive-thru. Each component visualizes real-time vehicle progression data for its respective zone.

ðŸ’¡ Further logic as to how cars are displayed can be found in external documentation.

Racetrack Components (Payment, Deliver, Pull Forward, Order Zone, Waiting Zone)

Description: Individual components of the full racetrack visualization, focusing on specific sections of the drive-thru.
Locations Covered:
  • Racetrack: Payment
  • Racetrack: Deliver
  • Racetrack: Pull Forward
  • Racetrack: Order Zone
  • Racetrack: Waiting Zone
How it is calculated: Visualizes real-time vehicle progression data for the respective zone, likely pulling from `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}` for average times and other live event topics for positions.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (e.g., `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}` and other live event topics).
Frequency of update: Real-time.

Limitations: Each is part of a larger racetrack visualization; detailed logic is external.

Full Racetrack

Description: Displays the complete racetrack visualization, combining all individual components.
How it is calculated: Combines real-time vehicle progression data from all relevant zones into a single view.
Source of data: IoT/MQTT (various topics for individual zones, e.g., `/eyeq/rolling/{fingermark_id}`).
Frequency of update: Real-time.
Clients currently using: TBD
Limitations: Logic details are external.
Must Have Widgets

There are a few widgets that each dashboard must have. These are used to identify version numbers of the dashboard, identify the current user logged in and used for reporting. These widgets cannot be deleted and do not appear in the widget library, but they can be resized and moved around the dashboard.

-Version

-StoreDetails

-QRCodeError

Alerting

This section describes the alerting capabilities of the dashboard, which trigger based on specific metrics and thresholds.

Restrictions

Widgets can be restricted to specific clients only. For example, all widgets relating to Thruput are restricted to KFC stores as it is a metric they only use.

Most widgets are unrestricted to clients and all terminology is adapted based on the client's preference.

Customization

All widgets can be moved and resized in the designer. This is done with a simple drag and drop functionality:

All widgets that a user is able to access are shown on the left-hand side of the screen, split into their various categories.

Widgets can be removed and added at users preference to design a dashboard that suits their specific needs.

Additional Widget Options:

  • Some widgets have additional options; by selecting the widget and clicking the widget configuration on the left, a drawer will open up with additional information.
  • The user can label the display title of the widget or even change how the information is displayed, i.e., the Order Average widget can be split into displaying the average times for lane 1 and 2 rather than a combined average.
Designer Options

The designer also has additional options along the top that allow the user to edit more general functionalities:

Renaming

Description: Each dashboard design can be renamed.

Select Dashboard

Description: Iterate through all dashboards the store has to edit.

My Screens

Description: Show all Chromeboxes currently configured to that store. From here the user can assign which dashboard the Chromebox should display and reboot those devices.

Templates

Description: If a user does not want to create a dashboard from scratch, they can select from templates designed by popular demand.

Store Settings

Description: Allow the user to alter various settings for the dashboard, e.g., display all times in minutes and seconds, set colour thresholds for targets.

Reset

Description: Undo all changes that have been made.

Clear All

Description: Clear the dashboard to empty except for the must-have widgets.

Save and Publish

Description: Save all changes and submit them to DynamoDB to be used in production. All screens currently pointing to those dashboards will update to the latest display after a few minutes. No reboot required.
